     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
       Features
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_disk_encryption_software&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Features">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        Hidden containers
       </b>
       : Whether hidden containers (an encrypted container (A) within another encrypted container (B) so the existence of container A can not be established)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         52
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       can be created for
       <a href="/wiki/Deniable_encryption" title="Deniable encryption">
        deniable encryption
       </a>
       . Note that some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Block_cipher_modes_of_operation" title="Block cipher modes of operation">
        modes of operation
       </a>
       like CBC with a plain IV can be more prone to
       <a href="/wiki/Watermarking_attack" title="Watermarking attack">
        watermarking attacks
       </a>
       than others.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Pre-boot authentication
       </b>
       : Whether authentication can be required before booting the computer, thus allowing one to encrypt the
       <a href="/wiki/Boot_disk" title="Boot disk">
        boot disk
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Single_sign-on" title="Single sign-on">
         Single sign-on
        </a>
       </b>
       : Whether credentials provided during pre-boot authentication will automatically log the user into the host operating system, thus preventing
       <a href="/wiki/Password_fatigue" title="Password fatigue">
        password fatigue
       </a>
       and reducing the need to remember multiple passwords.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Custom authentication
       </b>
       : Whether custom authentication mechanisms can be implemented with third-party applications.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2011)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Multiple keys
       </b>
       : Whether an encrypted volume can have more than one active
       <a href="/wiki/Key_(cryptography)" title="Key (cryptography)">
        key
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Passphrase strengthening
       </b>
       : Whether
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Key_strengthening" title="Key strengthening">
        key strengthening
       </a>
       is used with plain text passwords to frustrate
       <a href="/wiki/Dictionary_attack" title="Dictionary attack">
        dictionary attacks
       </a>
       , usually using
       <a href="/wiki/PBKDF2" title="PBKDF2">
        PBKDF2
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Hardware acceleration
       </b>
       : Whether dedicated
       <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_accelerator" title="Cryptographic accelerator">
        cryptographic accelerator
       </a>
       expansion cards can be taken advantage of.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Trusted_Platform_Module" title="Trusted Platform Module">
         Trusted Platform Module
        </a>
       </b>
       : Whether the implementation can use a TPM
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryptoprocessor" title="Cryptoprocessor">
        cryptoprocessor
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Filesystems
       </b>
       : what filesystems are supported.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Two-factor_authentication" title="Two-factor authentication">
         Two-factor authentication
        </a>
       </b>
       : Whether optional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_tokens" title="Security tokens">
        security tokens
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hardware_Security_Module" title="Hardware Security Module">
        hardware security modules
       </a>
       , such as Aladdin eToken and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smart_cards" title="Smart cards">
        smart cards
       </a>
       ) are supported (for example using
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PKCS11" title="PKCS11">
        PKCS#11
       </a>
       )
      </li>
     </ul>
     <table class="wikitable sortable" style="width: 100%; text-align: center; font-size: smaller; table-layout: fixed;">

      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-BitLockerFS-62">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-BitLockerFS_62-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Windows 7 introduces Bitlocker-To-Go which supports NTFS, FAT32 or exFAT, however for hard drive encryption,
         <a href="/wiki/Windows_Vista" title="Windows Vista">
          Windows Vista
         </a>
         and later are limited to be installable only on NTFS volumes
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-BitLocker2F-63">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-BitLocker2F_63-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         BitLocker can be used with a TPM PIN + external USB key for two-factor authentication
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-dm-cryptTPM-75">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-dm-cryptTPM_75-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         An external tool can be used to read the key from the TPM and then have the key passed on to dm-crypt/LUKS via the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_input" title="Standard input">
          standard input
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-TrueCryptMystery-102">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-TrueCryptMystery_102-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The current situation around TrueCrypt project is controversial. On 28.05.2014 after many years of development and broad usage the open-source (although anonymous) project was suddenly stopped, and all previous official materials and complete (encrypt/decrypt) binaries were withdrawn from its website citing some "unfixed security issues" and Windows XP end of support. The technical information herein is valid only for previous versions of TrueCrypt (v7.1a and some earlier). The latest available version (v7.2) is decrypt only, its authenticity and actual reasons behind the move are unclear, and its usage is not recommended.
         <a class="external free" href="http://www.zdnet.com/truecrypt-quits-inexplicable-7000029994/" rel="nofollow">
          http://www.zdnet.com/truecrypt-quits-inexplicable-7000029994/
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Layering">
       Layering
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_disk_encryption_software&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Layering">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For more details on this topic, see
      <a href="/wiki/Encryption_layer_in_storage_stack" title="Encryption layer in storage stack">
       Encryption layer in storage stack
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        Whole disk
       </b>
       : Whether the whole physical disk or logical volume can be encrypted, including the partition tables and master boot record. Note that this does not imply that the encrypted disk can be used as the boot disk itself; refer to "pre-boot authentication" in the features comparison table.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Partition
       </b>
       : Whether individual
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disk_partition" title="Disk partition">
        disk partitions
       </a>
       can be encrypted.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        File
       </b>
       : Whether the encrypted container can be stored in a file (usually implemented as encrypted
       <a href="/wiki/Loop_device" title="Loop device">
        loop devices
       </a>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Swap space
       </b>
       : Whether the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swap_space" title="Swap space">
        swap space
       </a>
       (called a "pagefile" on Windows) can be encrypted individually/explicitly.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Hibernation file
       </b>
       : Whether the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hibernate_(OS_feature)" title="Hibernate (OS feature)">
        hibernation file
       </a>
       is encrypted (if hibernation is supported).
      </li>
     </ul>
     <table class="wikitable sortable" style="width: 100%; text-align: center; font-size: smaller; table-layout: fixed;">

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Modes_of_operation">
       Modes of operation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_disk_encryption_software&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modes of operation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For more details on this topic, see
      <a href="/wiki/Disk_encryption_theory" title="Disk encryption theory">
       Disk encryption theory
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <p>
      Different modes of operation supported by the software. Note that an encrypted volume can only use one mode of operation.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        CBC with predictable IVs
       </b>
       : The CBC (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cipher_block_chaining" title="Cipher block chaining">
        cipher block chaining
       </a>
       ) mode where
       <a href="/wiki/Initialization_vector" title="Initialization vector">
        initialization vectors
       </a>
       are statically derived from the sector number and are not secret; this means that IVs are re-used when overwriting a sector and the vectors can easily be guessed by an attacker, leading to
       <a href="/wiki/Watermarking_attack" title="Watermarking attack">
        watermarking attacks
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        CBC with secret IVs
       </b>
       : The CBC mode where initialization vectors are statically derived from the encryption key and sector number. The IVs are secret, but they are re-used with overwrites. Methods for this include ESSIV and encrypted sector numbers (CGD).
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        CBC with random per-sector keys
       </b>
       : The CBC mode where random keys are generated for each sector when it is written to, thus does not exhibit the typical weaknesses of CBC with re-used initialization vectors. The individual sector keys are stored on disk and encrypted with a master key. (See
       <a href="/wiki/GBDE" title="GBDE">
        GBDE
       </a>
       for details)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        LRW
       </b>
       : The Liskov-Rivest-Wagner tweakable narrow-block mode, a mode of operation specifically designed for disk encryption. Superseded by the more secure XTS mode due to security concerns.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         118
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Disk_encryption_theory#XEX-based_tweaked-codebook_mode_with_ciphertext_stealing_.28XTS.29" title="Disk encryption theory">
         XTS
        </a>
       </b>
       : XEX-based Tweaked CodeBook mode (TCB) with CipherText Stealing (CTS), the
       <a href="/wiki/IEEE_P1619" title="IEEE P1619">
        SISWG
       </a>
       (IEEE P1619) standard for disk encryption.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <table class="wikitable sortable" style="width: 100%; text-align: center; font-size: smaller; table-layout: fixed;">
      <tr>
       <th>
        Name
       </th>
       <th>

       </th>

       </th>
       <th>

       </th>

       </th>

       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-yes" style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        Yes
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr class="sortbottom">
       <th>
        Name
       </th>
       <th>
        CBC w/ predictable IVs
       </th>
       <th>
        CBC w/ secret IVs
       </th>
       <th>
        CBC w/ random per-sector keys
       </th>
       <th>
        LRW
       </th>
       <th>
        XTS
       </th>
      </tr>
     </table>

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComparison+of+disk+encryption+software&amp;rft.btitle=New+features+in+BestCrypt+version+8&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.jetico.com%2Fbc8_web_help%2Fhtml%2F03_new_features%2F01_new_features.htm&amp;rft.pub=Jetico&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-125">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-125">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.jetico.com/bcve_web_help/html/01_introduction/04_new_in_version.htm" rel="nofollow">
           "New features in version 2"
          </a>
          . Jetico
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2009-03-01
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComparison+of+disk+encryption+software&amp;rft.btitle=New+features+in+version+2&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.jetico.com%2Fbcve_web_help%2Fhtml%2F01_introduction%2F04_new_in_version.htm&amp;rft.pub=Jetico&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Fergusson-126">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-Fergusson_126-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Fergusson_126-1">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             b
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation journal">
          Niels Fergusson (August 2006).
          <a class="external text" href="http://download.microsoft.com/download/0/2/3/0238acaf-d3bf-4a6d-b3d6-0a0be4bbb36e/BitLockerCipher200608.pdf" rel="nofollow">
           "AES-CBC + Elephant Diffuser: A Disk Encryption Algorithm for Windows Vista"
          </a>
          <span style="font-size:85%;">
           (PDF)
          </span>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
           Microsoft
          </a>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2008-02-22
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComparison+of+disk+encryption+software&amp;rft.aulast=Niels+Fergusson&amp;rft.au=Niels+Fergusson&amp;rft.btitle=AES-CBC+%2B+Elephant+Diffuser%3A+A+Disk+Encryption+Algorithm+for+Windows+Vista&amp;rft.date=August+2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fdownload.microsoft.com%2Fdownload%2F0%2F2%2F3%2F0238acaf-d3bf-4a6d-b3d6-0a0be4bbb36e%2FBitLockerCipher200608.pdf&amp;rft.pub=Microsoft&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-127">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-127">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://netbsd.gw.com/cgi-bin/man-cgi?cgd+4+NetBSD-current" rel="nofollow">
           "man 4 cgd in NetBSD-current"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           NetBSD current manual page on CGD
          </i>
          . 2006-03-11
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2006-12-24
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComparison+of+disk+encryption+software&amp;rft.atitle=man+4+cgd+in+NetBSD-current&amp;rft.date=2006-03-11&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnetbsd.gw.com%2Fcgi-bin%2Fman-cgi%3Fcgd%2B4%2BNetBSD-current&amp;rft.jtitle=NetBSD+current+manual+page+on+CGD&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-128">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-128">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Containers created with TrueCrypt versions 1.0 through 4.0 use CBC.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-129">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-129">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Containers created with TrueCrypt versions 4.1 through 4.3a use LRW, and support CBC for opening legacy containers only.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-130">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-130">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Containers created with CipherShed or TrueCrypt versions 5.0+ use XTS, and support LRW/CBC for opening legacy containers only.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-cryptoapi-lrw-131">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-cryptoapi-lrw_131-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Starting with Linux kernel version 2.6.20, CryptoAPI supports the LRW mode:
         <a class="external free" href="http://lwn.net/Articles/213650/" rel="nofollow">
          http://lwn.net/Articles/213650/
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-132">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-132">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://support.apple.com/kb/HT4790" rel="nofollow">
           "OS X Lion: About FileVault 2"
          </a>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2011-01-03
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComparison+of+disk+encryption+software&amp;rft.btitle=OS+X+Lion%3A+About+FileVault+2&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsupport.apple.com%2Fkb%2FHT4790&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">

          <span style="display:none;">

          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         For Scramdisk containers
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-sd4l-tc4-135">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-sd4l-tc4_135-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         For Truecrypt 4 containers
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-sd4l-tc5-6-136">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

          <a href="#cite_ref-sd4l-tc5-6_136-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         For Truecrypt 5 and 6 containers
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-137">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-137">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <a class="external text" href="http://marc.info/?l=openbsd-cvs&amp;m=121302798322835&amp;w=2" rel="nofollow">
          Commit enabling AES XTS
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-138">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-138">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Containers created with TrueCrypt versions 1.0 through 4.0 use CBC.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-139">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-139">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Containers created with TrueCrypt versions 4.1 through 4.3a use LRW, and support CBC for opening legacy containers only.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-140">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-140">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Containers created with TrueCrypt versions 5.0 or later use XTS, and support LRW/CBC for opening legacy containers only.
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
